$(window).load(function(){
	if ($('#user_login_control').is(':empty')){
	$.ajax({
		url: "http://reason.com/ajax/commenthandle",
		dataType: 'json',
		success: function(data) {
			$(document).trigger('loginStatus', [data]);
			$(document).trigger('adminview',[data]);
		},
		error: function(xhr, textStatus){
			var data = { logged_in:null, error:textStatus };
			$(document).trigger('loginStatus', [data]);
		}
	});

	$('.commentsheading &gt; span &gt; a').click(function(){
		document.location.hash = 'comment';
	});
	}
});


$(document).ready(function(){
	$.ajax({
		url: "http://reason.com/ajax/commenthandle",
		dataType: 'json',
		success: function(data) {
			$(document).trigger('loginStatus', [data]);
			$(document).trigger('adminview',[data]);
		},
		error: function(xhr, textStatus){
			var data = { logged_in:null, error:textStatus };
			$(document).trigger('loginStatus', [data]);
		}
	});

	$('.commentsheading &gt; span &gt; a').click(function(){
		document.location.hash = 'comment';
	});

	if (window.location.hash.match(/^#comment/)) {
			var cctrl = $('.commentcontrol'), cctnr = $('#commentcontainer');
			cctrl.addClass('open');
			cctnr.show();
			$('#commentform.cancomment').show();
		
	}else{
			var cctrl = $('.commentcontrol'), cctnr = $('#commentcontainer');
			cctnr.hide();
			cctrl.removeClass('open');
			cctrl.one('click', function(e) {
				cctrl.addClass('open');
				cctnr.show();
				$('#commentform.cancomment').show();
			});
	}
	if($.cookie('fontSize')) {
		var fontSize = $.cookie('fontSize');
 		$('article.post').css({'font-size':fontSize});
 		$('ul.posts').css({'font-size':fontSize});
 	}

	// SIDR PANELS

	$('#mobile-nav-toggle').unbind('onclick');
	$('#mobile-nav-toggle').sidr({
		displace: false,
		name: 'sidr-main',
		source: '#site-navigation',
		side:'right'
	});
	jQuery('#sidr-main .sidr-class-closemenu a').click(function(){
		jQuery.sidr('close', 'sidr-main');
		jQuery('.small-share').show();
	});
	jQuery('.container_24').click(function(){
		jQuery.sidr('close', 'sidr-main');
	});
	jQuery('#mobile-nav-toggle').click(function(){
		jQuery('.small-share').hide();
	});


	$('#mobile-trending-toggle').unbind('onclick');
	jQuery('#mobile-trending-toggle').sidr({
		displace: false,
		name: 'sidr-trending',
		source: '#trending-navigation',
		side: 'left'
	});
	jQuery('#sidr-trending .sidr-class-closemenu a').click(function(){

        jQuery('.small-share').show();
	});
	jQuery('.container_24').click(function(){
		jQuery.sidr('close', 'sidr-trending');
	});
	jQuery('#mobile-trending-toggle').click(function(){
		jQuery('.small-share').hide();
	});
	jQuery(window).resize(function () {
		if (jQuery(window).width() &gt; 700) {
			jQuery.sidr('close', 'sidr-main');
			jQuery.sidr('close', 'sidr-trending');
		}
	});

	// let's do this in jquery so we're sure it's stacked
	$('textarea').focus( function() {
		jQuery.sidr('close', 'sidr-main');
		jQuery.sidr('close', 'sidr-trending');
	});
	// $.sidr('open', 'sidr-main');

	function setScaleable(x) {
		originalval = $('head meta[name=viewport]').attr('content');
		newval = originalval.replace(/(user-scalable=)\d{1,9}/g, '$1'+x);
		if (originalval.localeCompare(newval)) {
			$('head meta[name=viewport]').attr('content', newval);
		} else {
			$('head meta[name=viewport]').attr('content', originalval+', user-scalable='+x);
		}
	}

	//we don't want the screen to scale up when we select a text item, so we're going to prevent it by turning it on and off as we enter and leave
	$('textarea, input').on('focusin', function() {
		setScaleable(0);
	});

	$('textaream, input').on('focusout', function() {
		setScaleable(1);
	});

	// there's some visual element eh when people leave the screen, possibly because of fixed position
	// and element destruction order. We're going to simply hide these items on the way out to make sure
	// they don't jump around
	$( window ).unload(function() {
  		$('#nav1').hide();
  		$('#sidr-main').hide();
  		$('#sidr-trending').hide();
	});


	$("a#sidr-id-fontbigger").click(function() {
 		$('ul.posts').css('font-size', function(index,value) {
 			var fontSize = parseInt(value) + 1 + 'px';
	 		$.cookie('fontSize',fontSize, { path: '/', expires: 7 });
	 		return fontSize;
 		});
 		$('#right-col').css('font-size', function(index,value) {

	 		$.cookie('fontSize',fontSize, { path: '/', expires: 7 });
	 		return fontSize;

  		$('article.post').css('font-size', function(index,value) {
 			var fontSize = parseInt(value) + 1 + 'px';
	 		$.cookie('fontSize',fontSize, { path: '/', expires: 7 });
	 		return fontSize;
 		});
	});

	$("a#sidr-id-fontsmaller").click(function() {
 		$('ul.posts').css('font-size', function(index,value) {
 			var fontSize = parseInt(value) - 1 + 'px';
	 		$.cookie('fontSize',fontSize, { path: '/', expires: 7 });

window.USERSTATE = {logged_in:null};
$(document).bind('loginStatus', function(e, d) {
	$.extend(window.USERSTATE, d);
});

	$(document).bind('adminview', function(e, d) {
		if(d.isadmin){
			$("body").addClass("adminlogin");
			window.ADMININFO = JSONObject= {
				"baseurl":"http://reason.com/",
				"showeditbutton":1,
				"showadminbar":1,
				"showcommentcontrols":1,
				"usersettingsurl":"http://reason.com/admin/users//modify",
				"commentactions" : 0};
			$.getScript("/media/js/navtools.js");
		}
	});

function updateCountdowns() {
	editbuttons = $('button.comment_edit:visible');
	if (editbuttons.length) {
		editbuttons.each(function() {
			timeremaining = $(this).data('editwindow-remaining');
			if (--timeremaining &lt; 0) {
				$(this).text('edit timer expired');
				$(this).fadeOut(); //no need for further time update; we only poll visibles
			} else {
				$(this).text('edit ('+timeremaining+' seconds remaining)');
				$(this).data('editwindow-remaining', timeremaining);
			}
		})
	} else {
		//no reason to keep this running when there's nothing to update
		clearInterval(countdownTimer);
	}
}

var countdownTimer = null;

$(document).bind('loginStatus', function(e,d){
	servertime = Number(d.unixtime);
	editing_window_seconds = Number(d.editing_window_seconds);
	if (d.logged_in) {
		userID = d.user_id;
		var handle = $("#user_login_control")
		.html('&lt;p&gt;You are currently logged in as: &lt;strong&gt;&lt;a href="http://reason.com/users/manage" class="handle"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;. &lt;a href="http://reason.com/users/logout"&gt;&lt;span&gt;Sign Out&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;')
		.find('.handle')
		handle.text(d.handle)
		handle.attr('href', handle.attr('href')+'/'+userID);
		//look for all the editable comments by this user
		$('div#commentcontainer li[data-user-id='+userID+']').each(function( index ) {
			commenttimestamp = Number($(this).data('comment-timestamp'));
			elapsedtime = servertime - commenttimestamp;
			if (elapsedtime &lt; editing_window_seconds) {
				secondsremaining = editing_window_seconds - elapsedtime;
				$(this).find('button.comment_edit').show().data('editwindow-remaining', secondsremaining);
			}
		});
		countdownTimer = setInterval(updateCountdowns, 1E3);
	} else {
		$("#user_login_control").html('&lt;a href="http://reason.com/users/login"&gt;&lt;span&gt;Login&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; or &lt;a href="http://reason.com/users/register"&gt;&lt;span&gt;Sign-up&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;');
	}
});

(function(){
	var threadedCommentRepliesActive=null;
	var cb = $('#commentcontainer');

	function cmtLoginStatusHandler(e,d) {
		var lc = $('#commentform'), clr = $('.comment_login_require');
		if (d.logged_in) {
			clr.hide();
			lc.addClass('cancomment');
			lc.find('.logged_in_as').remove();
			var handle = lc.children('form')
			.prepend('&lt;div class="logged_in_as"&gt;&lt;p&gt;You are currently logged in as &lt;a href="http://reason.com/users/manage/'+d.user_id+'" class="handle"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. Not you? &lt;a href="http://reason.com/users/logout"&gt;Sign out&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;')
			.find('.handle');
			handle.text(d.handle);
			handle.attr('a', handle.attr('a')+'/'+d.user_id);
			lc.show();
			threadedCommentReplies(true);
			editComments(true);
		} else if (d.logged_in===false) {
			clr.show();
			lc.removeClass('cancomment');
			threadedCommentReplies(false);
		} else {
			clr.html('&lt;p&gt;Oops, something went wrong and we can\'t tell if you\'re logged in. Please referesh and try again.&lt;/p&gt;');
		}
	}

	function threadedCommentReplies(activate){
		var cb = $('#commentcontainer');
		if (activate) {
			cb.find('.comment_reply').show();
			cb.find('.comment_reply_msg').hide();
			if (!threadedCommentRepliesActive &amp;&amp; (typeof(CommentReplyForm) !== "undefined")) {
				var template = CommentReplyForm.preparetemplate('commentform');
				var crf = new CommentReplyForm(template);
				crf.bindHandlers('li.com-block button.comment_reply');
				var previewurl = $('#commentform form').attr('action').replace(/\/post$/, '/preview');
				CommentPreview.bindHandlers(template, template.find(':button.preview'), previewurl);
				CommentPreview.bindHandlers($('#commentform'), $('#commentform :button.preview'), previewurl);
			}
		} else {
			cb.find('.comment_reply').hide();
			cb.find('.comment_reply_msg').show();
			cb.find('.leave-comment').hide();
		}
	}

	function editComments(activate) {
		var cb = $('#commentcontainer');
		if (activate) {
			//we find only the ones made visible during initialization; no reason to bind the rest.
			// active_edit_buttons = $('button.comment_edit:visible');
			if (typeof(CommentEditForm) !== "undefined") {
				var template = CommentEditForm.preparetemplate('commenteditform');
				var crf = new CommentEditForm(template);
				crf.bindHandlers('button.comment_edit:visible');
			}
		} else {
			cb.find('button.comment_edit').hide();
		}
	}
	$(document).bind('loginStatus', cmtLoginStatusHandler);


})();

          John Stossel
         </a>
         | February 25, 2010

            <div id="spritzer_139539" style="display:none;">

            <script>
             var SpritzSettings = {
									clientId: "eb6c148c66f0e0a73",
									redirectUri: "http://reason.com/login_success.html"
								};
								$(function () {
								    var spritzController = null;
									function spritz_139539() {
										function spritz_139539_visibility() {
											$('#spritzer_139539').toggle();
											$('#clicktospritz_139539').toggle();
										}
										function spritz_139539init() {
										    var onSpritzifySuccess = function(spritzText) {
												console.log('Spritzify success');
										        spritzController.startSpritzing(spritzText);
										    };
										    var onSpritzifyError = function(error) {
										        alert("Unable to Spritz: " + error.message);
										    };

											var customOptions = {
											        placeholderText:    { startText: 'Nope' },
											        header: 			{	login: false,
											        						close: true,
											        						closeHandler: spritz_139539_visibility },
													// redicleWidth:       300,
											        redicleHeight:      76      // Specify Redicle height
											};

											if (spritzController === null) {
												// Construct a SpritzController passing the customization options
												spritzController = new SPRITZ.spritzinc.SpritzerController(customOptions);
												// Attach the controller's container to this page's "spritzer" container
												spritzController.attach($('#spritzer_139539'));
										    }										    // this would be the most basic and inclusive way, but we really want to avoid reading photo captions etc
										    // text = $('#spritzer_139539').parents('article').find('div.postcontent').text();
										    var text = '';
										    var textNodes = $('#spritzer_139539').parents('article').find('div.postcontent').find('p');

										    // we want to exclude spans since they're how our image captions are enclosed
										    for (var i = 0; i &lt; textNodes.length; i++) {
												text += $(textNodes[i])
												    .clone()    //clone the element
												    .children() //select all the children
												    .remove('span')   //remove all the children
												    .end()  //again go back to selected element
												    .text() + '\n\n';
										        // text += $(textNodes[i]).text() + '\n\n';
										    }
											var locale = "en_us;";
										    // Send to SpritzEngine to translate
										    SpritzClient.spritzify(text, locale, onSpritzifySuccess, onSpritzifyError);
										}

										$(document).on('spritz_loaded', function() {
											console.log('Spritz loaded');
										   // Code that depends on a an initialized SpritzClient goes here
											spritz_139539_visibility();
											spritz_139539init();


										}); //end spritz_loaded

										if (typeof SpritzClient === 'undefined') {
											$.getScript('//sdk.spritzinc.com/js/1.2/js/spritz.min.js', function() {
												console.log('Spritz.min.js loaded');
											});
										} else {
											spritz_139539_visibility();
											spritz_139539init();
										}
									};
									$('#clicktospritz_139539').click(function() {spritz_139539(); return false;});
								})
            </script>
           </li>
           <li class="clear">
           </li>
          </ul>
         </div>
        </aside>
        <div class="clear">
        </div>
        <div class="audio" style="display:none;">
        </div>
       </header>
       <!--&lt;div class='google-ad'&gt;-->
       <!--&lt;/div&gt;-->
       <div class="p402_premium">
        <div class="entry postcontent">
         <p>
          People suffer and die because the government "protects" us. It
should protect us less and respect our liberty more.
         </p>
         <section class="asidecontainer p402_hide desktop-only">
          <aside class="relatedinfo">
           <section class="relatedarticles">
            <header>
             <h3>
              RELATED ARTICLES
             </h3>
            </header>
            <ul>
             <li>
              <h4>
               <a href="http://reason.com/blog/2015/07/06/its-2015-and-the-british-government-is-c">
                Its 2015, and the British Government Is Considering Expanding the Drug War Faster
               </a>
              </h4>
              <p class="meta">
               <a href="http://reason.com/people/scott-shackford">
                Scott Shackford
               </a>
               <span class="pipe">

               <time datetime="2015-07-06T18:25:00+00:00">
                7.06.15
               </time>
              </p>
             </li>
             <li>
              <h4>
               <a href="http://reason.com/reasontv/2015/06/23/5-more-drug-psas-that-tried-to-scare-the">
                5 More Drug PSAs That Tried to Scare the Sh*t Out of Us (But Didn't)
               </a>
              </h4>
              <p class="meta">
               <a href="http://reason.com/people/paul-detrick">
                Paul Detrick
               </a>
               <span class="pipe">
                |
               </span>
               <time datetime="2015-06-23T15:17:00+00:00">
                6.23.15
               </time>
              </p>
             </li>
             <li>
              <h4>
               <a href="http://reason.com/blog/2015/06/21/vid-did-these-5-drug-psas-stop-drug-use">
                VID: Did These 5 Drug PSAs Stop Drug Use? Not Even Close.
               </a>
              </h4>
              <p class="meta">
               <a href="http://reason.com/people/paul-detrick">
                Paul Detrick
               </a>
               <span class="pipe">
                |
               </span>
               <time datetime="2015-06-21T21:00:00+00:00">
                6.21.15
               </time>
              </p>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </section>
           <section class="morearticles">
            <h3>
             MORE ARTICLES BY
             <a href="http://reason.com/people/john-stossel/all">
              John Stossel
             </a>
            </h3>
            <ul>
             <li>
              <h4>
               <a href="http://reason.com/archives/2015/07/08/lots-of-democrats-want-socialism">
                Lots of Democrats Want Socialism
               </a>
              </h4>
              <p class="meta">
               <time datetime="2015-07-08T04:05:00+00:00">
                7.08.15 12:05 am
               </time>
              </p>
             </li>
             <li>
              <h4>
               <a href="http://reason.com/archives/2015/07/01/corporations-have-become-hollywoods-go-t">
                Corporations Have Become Hollywood's Go-To Villians
               </a>
              </h4>
              <p class="meta">
               <time datetime="2015-07-01T04:05:00+00:00">
                7.01.15 12:05 am
               </time>
              </p>
             </li>
             <li>
              <h4>
               <a href="http://reason.com/archives/2015/06/24/instead-of-replacing-alexander-hamilton">
                Instead of Replacing Alexander Hamilton, Replace Federal Reserve Notes With Private Currency
               </a>
              </h4>
              <p class="meta">
               <time datetime="2015-06-24T04:05:00+00:00">
                6.24.15 12:05 am
               </time>
              </p>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </section>
           <section class="relatedtopics">
            <ul>
             <li>
              <a href="http://reason.com/tags/drug-policy">
               Drug Policy
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://reason.com/tags/regulation">
               Regulation
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://reason.com/tags/fda">
               FDA
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://reason.com/tags/obamacare">
               Obamacare
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </section>
          </aside>
         </section>
         <p>
          The most basic questions are: Who owns you, and who should
control what you put into your body? In what sense are you free if
you can't decide what medicines you will take?
         </p>
         <p>
          This will be the subject of my Fox Business program tonight.
         </p>
         <p>
          We'll hear from people like Bruce Tower. Tower has prostate
cancer. He wanted to take a drug that showed promise against his
cancer, but the Food and Drug Administration would not allow it.
One bureaucrat told him the government was protecting him from
dangerous side effects. Tower's outraged response was: "Side
effectswho cares? Every treatment I've had I've suffered from side
effects. If I'm terminal, it should be my option to endure any side
effects."
         </p>
         <p>
          Of course it should be his option. Why, in our "free" country,
do Americans meekly stand aside and let the state limit our
choices, even when we are dying?
         </p>
         <p>
          Dr. Alan Chow invented a retinal implant that helps some blind
people see (
          <a href="http://www.optobionics.com">
           optobionics.com
          </a>
          ). Demonstrating
that took seven years and cost $50 million dollars of FDA-approved
tests. But now the FDA wants still more tests. That third stage
will take another three years and cost $100 million. But Chow
doesn't have $100 million. He can't raise the money from investors
because the implant only helps some blind people. Potential
investors fear there are too few customers to justify their $100
million risk.
         </p>
         <div class="ym" id="ym_1044036704457308825">
         </div>
         <script type="text/javascript">
          (function(e,t){if(t._ym===void 0){t._ym="";var m=e.createElement("script");m.type="text/javascript",m.async=!0,m.src="//static.yieldmo.com/ym.m5.js",(e.getElementsByTagName("head")[0]||e.getElementsByTagName("body")[0]).appendChild(m)}else t._ym instanceof String||void 0===t._ym.chkPls||t._ym.chkPls()})(document,window);
         </script>
         <p>
          So Stephen Lonegan, who has a degenerative eye disease that
might be helped by the implant, can't have it. Instead, he will go
blind. The bureaucrats say their restrictions are for his own
safety. "There's nothing safe about going blind," he says. "I don't
want to be made safe by the FDA. I want it to be up to me to go to
Dr. Chow to make the decision myself."
         </p>
         <p>
          But it's not up to Lonegan and his doctor. It's up to the
autocrats of the Nanny State. Tonight, I will show my confrontation
with Terry Toigo of the FDA about that. She calmly and quietly
explained that such restrictions are necessary to protect the
integrity of the government's safety review process until I
shouted: "Why are you even involved? Let people try things!"
         </p>
         <p>
          She replied, "We don't think that's the best system for
patients, to enable people to just take whatever they want with
little information available about a drug."
         </p>
         <p>
          So people suffer and die when they might have lived longer, more
comfortable lives.
         </p>
         <p>
          The FDA's intrusion on our freedom is supplemented by another
agent of the Nanny State. The Drug Enforcement Agency's war on drug
dealers has led them to watch pain-management doctors like hawks.
Drugs like Vicodin and OxyContin provide wonderful pain relief. But
because they are also taken by "recreational" drug users, doctors
go to jail for prescribing quantities that the DEA considers
"inappropriate." As a result, pain specialists are scared into
underprescribing painkillers. Sick people suffer horrible pain
needlessly.
         </p>
         <p>
          Think I exaggerate? Check out the website of the
          <a href="http://www.aapsonline.org">
           American Association of Physicians and
Surgeons
          </a>
          (AAPS). It warns doctors not to go into pain
management. "Drug agents now set medical standards. ... There could
be years of harassment and legal fees," says the AAPS. Today, even
nursing-home patients, hardly candidates for drug gangs,
          <a href="http://tinyurl.com/yb4ykxg">
           don't get
          </a>
          pain relief they
need.
         </p>
         <p>
          The DEA told us that good doctors have nothing to worry about.
But Siobhan Reynolds, who started the Pain Relief Network (
          <a href="http://www.painreliefnetwork.org">
           painreliefnetwork.org
          </a>
          ) after
her late husband was unable to get sufficient pain medicine, says
the DEA's cherry-picked medical experts persuade juries that they
should jail any doctor who administers higher doses of pain relief
than the DEA's zealots think appropriate. News of those jail terms
spreads. Doctors learn to be stingy with pain meds.
         </p>
         <p>
          All drugs involve risk. In a free country, it should be up to
individuals, once we're adults, to make our own choices about those
risks. Patrick Henry didn't say, "Give me absolute safety, or give
me death." He said "liberty." That is what America is supposed to
be about.
         </p>
         <p>
          <em>
           John Stossel is host of
          </em>
          Stossel
          <em>
           on the Fox Business
Network. He's the author of
          </em>
          Give Me a Break
          <em>
           and of
          </em>
          Myth, Lies, and Downright Stupidity
          <em>
           . To find out more about
John Stossel, visit his site at
           <a href="http://www.johnstossel.com">
            johnstossel.com
           </a>
           .
          </em>
         </p>

           <!--Comment Body-->
           <div class="content">
            <p>
             "Comrades," he said, "I trust that every animal here appreciates
the
             <br/>
             sacrifice that Comrade Napoleon has made in taking this extra
labour upon
             <br/>
             himself. Do not imagine, comrades, that leadership is a pleasure!
On the
             <br/>
             contrary, it is a deep and heavy responsibility. No one believes
more
             <br/>
             firmly than Comrade Napoleon that all animals are equal. He would
be only
             <br/>
             too happy to let you make your decisions for yourselves. But
sometimes you
             <br/>
             might make the wrong decisions, comrades, and then where should we
be?
            </p>
           </div>

try the treatment. You just want to kill people so you can feel
better about yourself and avoid "deaths" that would probably be
avoided anyway.

           <div class="content">
            <p>
             "Perhaps they should try and fail accepted treatments
first."
            </p>
            <p>
             If they were going to die anyway, I would say they haven't lost
much. But not every treatment fails. Some treatments are
successful. And people die because they don't get them while they
wait for the FDA to approve them. Yes, if the treatment is a
failure, the people will die anyway. But in the cases where the new
drug or treatment is successful, the quicker it gets to the market
the more people it can save.
            </p>

           <!--Comment Body-->
           <div class="content">
            <p>
             They're ALL individual needs. The individuals who die because
they tried a treatment that hasn't gone through extensive testing
are individuals, and the individuals who die because they can't try
a drug that hasn't gone through extensive testing are individuals.
In fact, for the most part, it's the SAME individuals. What you're
saying is that the FDA should weigh the risks rather than the
individuals themselves. And that the FDA is so good at this that
they make better decisions for everyone than individuals could make
for themselves. This despite the fact that the FDA, just like every
government agency, reflects the interests of those most interested
in the regulations, namely doctors and drug companies. And that
large companies marketing existing drugs that can afford the
approval process would like nothing less than they would like new
drugs from small competitors.
            </p>
           </div>

           <div class="content">
            <p>
             "And thanks to the FDA ban on vioxx, people who suffer from
arthritis are now back taking huge amounts of aspirin that is
eating away at the lining of their stomachs."
            </p>
            <p>
             And since you brought up aspirin, it's worth noting that under
today's FDA regulations if aspirin was a new drug coming down the
pipeline you would absolutely need a prescription to obtain it due
to it's MOA. Also, many commonly prescribed drugs people have used
every day for years would not even get FDA approval today b/c of
the side effects. Phenytoin is a good example. Since this is my
line of work, this issue is particularly annoying to me. Every
single drug you take has side effects. The question is do those
side effects outweigh the benefits of taking the drug? If it is a
potentially life saving treatment I say no.
            </p>
           </div>

           <!--Comment Body-->
           <div class="content">
            <p>
             This is industry capture at its finest. The large drug companies
are better off if making new drugs is expensive, because not only
are they preventing smaller competitors from entering the market,
but they're also protecting the market for their existing drugs.
And since the only people who have the expertise to say whether a
drug is safe are people deeply involved in making and testing
drugs, e.g. people working for the large drug companies or who
might work for the large drug companies, the drug companies
interests get represented when deciding whether to approve a new
drug.
            </p>
           </div>

            <strong>

            </strong>
            <span class="pipe">
             |
            </span>
            <strong>
             <time datetime="2010-03-05T18:25:42+00:00">
              3.5.10 @ 1:25PM
             </time>
            </strong>
            <span class="pipe">
             |
            </span>
            <a class="permalink" href="#comment_1599248">
             #
            </a>
           </p>
           <!--Comment Body-->
           <div class="content">
            <p>
             Increasing a manufacturer's cost of manufacturing is not
necessarily good for their bottom line. Revenues need to exceed
costs. Bain and Co. report that the average cost of developing a
new drug is $1.7 billion, as of 2003. This means that if a monthly
prescription costs $1,000, then they have to sell 1.7 million of
them just to recapture R&amp;D costs, without any profit or
production cost. FDA blockage does not make pharmaceutical
companies more profitable. It makes it harder for them to clear
their costs. That same Bain study, found at
             <a href="http://www.bain.com/bainweb/About/press_release_detail.asp?id=14243&amp;menu_url=for_the_media.asp," rel="nofollow">
              http://www.bain.com/bainweb/Ab.....media.asp,
             </a>
             shows that the average annual return on investment in
pharmaceuticals is only a paltry 5%, quite low in comparison to
most industries. FDA hindrances on drug development cause drug
companies to be less profitable, while blocking many lifesaving
medications from being accessed by patients. I repeatedly read in
medical literature about drugs that are safer and more effective
than what is available in the U.S., but are not approved by the
FDA. Regardless of the practical points that I point out here, the
main point is that our government does not have the legitamate
authority to be making these decisions for us. Kudos, Mr. Stossell,
for making this point so well.
            </p>
           </div>

           <!--Comment Body-->
           <div class="content">
            <p>
             "Perhaps they should take less?"
            </p>
            <p>
             Sure take less and then suffer from debilitating pain. They
aren't taking the aspirin for fun and profit. They are taking it
because arthritis is a horrible disease.
            </p>
            <p>
             "Death from heart attacks is a minor side effect?"
            </p>
            <p>
             If your choices are:
            </p>
            <p>
             1. Suffer from horrible pain every day, or
            </p>
            <p>
             2. Take aspirin and know that you will in a few years destroy
your stomach and kidneys
            </p>
            <p>
             3. Take vioxx and have a slightly elevated risk of a heart
attack,
            </p>
            <p>
             the risk of a heart attack is when considered in context the
lesser side effect.
            </p>
            <p>
             It is called managing risk. We don't get to have the medicine
fairy come down and cure all of our ills. Sometimes you have to
take least bad option. And people like you are helping to ensure
that people have to take the worst option.
            </p>
           </div>

           <!--Comment Body-->
           <div class="content">
            <p>
             IIRC, Thalidomide had two different ways of crystallizing. One
way, it was completely safe for pregnant women and their babies.
the other caused birth defects. Either way, it was effective as a
sedative and anti-emetic.
            </p>
            <p>
             Furthermore, it is now being tested for numerous conditions. As
mentioined above, it is a fairly effective anti-emetic (which is
why it was given to pregnant women), and has promise against
certain types of cancer. I'm sure banning it really helped advance
the research on that.
            </p>
           </div>

             Yep, it exists as two different stereoisomers.
             <br/>
             One form would be good for treating morning sickness, and the other
inhibited fetal limb development.

in the body.

             And they did make morphine better by doing that. Diacetyl
morphine (aka Heroin) penetrates the BBB far more effectively than
morphine, and doesn't cause the (often fatal) histamine reaction in
the brain that morphine can. It's also about 5x more effective as a
pain killer than morphine. There was an Australian doctor who
posted on a thread a few months ago lamenting the fact that she had
to treat her patients with a much crappier and dangerous
pain-relief drug, all because of the WoD.
            </p>
            <p>
             That pain relief effectiveness also means it's much more
effective for people who want to get high, and Jeebus knows we
can't have that.
            </p>
           </div>
           <!--Comment actions (Reply/Login/Register)-->

           <!--Comment Body-->
           <div class="content">
            <p>
             Question: If someone decides to take Medicine X and dies, and
their family decides to sue the drug company because they think the
medicine was the cause of death, isn't the burden of proof on the
plaintiff to demonstrate this? How would they go about doing so? I
may well be wrong, but it seems they would have to commission and
pay for the testing procedures that the FDA currently mandates in
order to provide conclusive enough evidence to actually win a case
in court. Granted, the drug companies might elect to settle out of
court in order to avoid an excess of negative PR, but then you wind
up with a potentially dangerous medicine still on the market that
hasn't been proven to be either safe or dangerous.
            </p>
            <p>
             Not that I'm saying the FDA is awesome here, just that the idea
that the free market might not be entirely effective on its
own.
            </p>
           </div>

           <!--Comment Body-->
           <div class="content">
            <p>
             Re: Brian Trust,
            </p>
            <blockquote>
             Question: If someone decides to take Medicine X and
dies, and their family decides to sue the drug company because they
think the medicine was the cause of death, isn't the burden of
proof on the plaintiff to demonstrate this?
            </blockquote>
            <p>
             Yes, it is, because as you said: The person DECIDED to take
Medicine X.
            </p>
            <blockquote>
             How would they go about doing so?
            </blockquote>
            <p>
             The same as with everything else: The person that wants to prove
PAYS for it.
            </p>
            <blockquote>
             I may well be wrong, but it seems they would have to
commission and pay for the testing procedures that the FDA
currently mandates in order to provide conclusive enough evidence
to actually win a case in court.
            </blockquote>
            <p>
             That's no excuse to have the FDA. You mean have everybody else
pay so that a few plaintiffs can profit from the existence of the
FDA? That's immoral.
            </p>
           </div>

           <div class="content">
            <p>
             Troll, there is no "safe medical procedure". There are only less
risky ones. It is possible for you to die from someone putting an
IV in your arm. Tragic if that happens? Yes. But the risks are
there. Before a surgical procedure you have to sign off on the
risks...that they have been explained and you are aware of them.
You can refuse.
            </p>
            <p>
             Just thought I'd put that out there for general consumption. I
hear patients and their families talking about being "safe" with
medicine and go out of my way to educate them differently. Drives
me nuts.
            </p>

           <div class="content">
            <p>
             Fuck off Warren. Seriously fuck off. If you have a problem with
my posts, at least read the damned things. Go find one where I ever
defend the drug war.
            </p>
            <p>
             As far as experimental drugs, you argument is stupid. If you got
rid of the FDA tomorrow, that wouldn't mean that companies would
immediately start selling unproven drugs to anyone and everyone who
wants them. They still would be subject to tort law and have plenty
of motivation to ensure that their products worked and were not
harmful before they sold them. Further, drug companies want to
produce advanced drugs. That is their business. If giving out a
drug to everyone would destroy their ability to test its
effectiveness, they wouldn't do it. They would conduct trials first
and figure out if the stuff worked and make sure it was safe. The
difference would be that they would conduct the trials based on
their scientific judgment rather than spending millions and years
trying to convince an overly cautious FDA bureaucrat.
            </p>
            <p>
             It really takes a lot of nerve of you to make some snarky Fox
News comment about me, after making such a dumb ass argument for
the FDA. Pathetic.
            </p>

           <div class="content">
            <p>
             "Aware of the risks" is the key phrase here. You're assuming
that people are operating with perfect information. What if a Drug
company decides to use an unsafe or risky substance in order to cut
production costs but does not disclose the presence of that
substance by calling it "proprietary" or something? Acting on the
assumption that "oh they wouldn't do something to harm their
customers" would then be foolish at best. An obligation to disclose
production methods and ingredients seems essential to providing the
information required to make a proper choice.
            </p>

           <!--Comment Body-->
           <div class="content">
            <p>
             There is no such thing as perfect information. Ever. The thing
about medicine is that it is a constantly changing field. We find
out that drugs have effects we never knew existed and uses we
didn't suspect. But if someone is dying anyway and they want to
have a bit of hope rather than just waiting to check out, why do
you have a problem with excepting that experimental drug? Let them
be followed closely by their physician for side effects and the
like. Might make our understanding of that drug better.
            </p>
            <p>
             Just as an aside, how many of you guys posting here have ever
had to tell someone that you have nothing left to offer them and
that they're going to die? What if you had to tell them that
knowing that an experimental treatment existed that showed great
promise and probably would get approved in 3 months? The patient
has 2 months. When you do that, I'll be happy to hear your views.
I'm sure they'll be interesting.
            </p>

           <div class="content">
            <p>
             Insurance companies would probably still not cover for
experimental treatments. However, once the FDA is gone,
experimental or novel treatments would be more affordable since the
producers would not have to jump through burning hoops just to get
approval for testing, let alone distribution.
            </p>

some moms have their panties all bunched up over some expensive
drug that treats some rare childhood cancer. They are upset that
the evil pharmaceutical company charges 20K per treatment. They
want to force the company to sell it cheaper as it obviously
"gouges" the poor cancer kids. At $1 BILLION per drug, they charge
what they charge. People are so short sighted.
            </p>

           <!--Comment Body-->
           <div class="content">
            <p>
             The underlying bigger picture: Some Constitutional law experts
have white papered their opinions as to the unconstitutionality of
administrative law, i.e. FDA, DEA, etc. Some say admin law violates
the separation of powers clause. Google it. Elected members of the
House and/or Senate have the constitutional authority to make laws,
not political appointees. Thus, when a federal agent (of any
department) enforces a rule some bureaucrat made in his respective
agency, isn't it that federal government employee who is the
potential lawbreaker, instead of the taxpaying consumer?
            </p>
           </div>

            <p>
             As to your anecdote about how bacteria would be less evolvable
if only the CDC got out of the way and let the market do that thing
it does--I think we both want doctors and other experts deciding
how to best ration antibiotics, right? But certainly not because
people are TOO THOOPID to understand the microbiology cutting
edge.
            </p>
           </div>

"terminal illness"; you are clearly unfamiliar with that term.
            </p>
            <p>
             Sure drugs kill people, apparently adverse reactions to
prescription drugs results in 32,000 deaths in the US annually.
Contrast that with the 435,000 people killed by tobacco, 365,000
deaths due to poor diet and physical inactivity, 85,000 due to
alcohol and 26,347 due to vehicle accidents. Should the government
prohibit cigarettes, alcohol, cars and fat people in the name of
protecting people? If the answer is no then why the double
standard with prescription drugs?
             <a href="http://drugwarfacts.org/cms/?q=node/30">
              Data
             </a>
             . Interesting side
note: the number of deaths due to marijuana annually: ZERO.
            </p>

	l[0]='&gt;';l[1]='a';l[2]='/';l[3]='&lt;';l[4]='|110';l[5]='|101';l[6]='|32';l[7]='|97';l[8]='|105';l[9]='|120';l[10]='|32';l[11]='|111';l[12]='|97';l[13]='|103';l[14]='&gt;';l[15]='"';l[16]='|109';l[17]='|111';l[18]='|99';l[19]='|46';l[20]='|104';l[21]='|116';l[22]='|111';l[23]='|109';l[24]='|109';l[25]='|97';l[26]='|109';l[27]='|103';l[28]='|110';l[29]='|105';l[30]='|99';l[31]='|110';l[32]='|97';l[33]='|100';l[34]='|64';l[35]='|114';l[36]='|101';l[37]='|98';l[38]='|105';l[39]='|114';l[40]='|99';l[41]='|98';l[42]='|117';l[43]='|115';l[44]='|108';l[45]='|97';l[46]='|116';l[47]='|105';l[48]='|103';l[49]='|105';l[50]='|100';l[51]=':';l[52]='o';l[53]='t';l[54]='l';l[55]='i';l[56]='a';l[57]='m';l[58]='"';l[59]='=';l[60]='f';l[61]='e';l[62]='r';l[63]='h';l[64]=' ';l[65]='a';l[66]='&lt;';
	for (var i = l.length-1; i &gt;= 0; i=i-1){
	if (l[i].substring(0, 1) == '|') document.write("&amp;#"+unescape(l[i].substring(1))+";");
	else document.write(unescape(l[i]));}
	//]]&gt;
             </script>
            </strong>

            <p>

            </p>
            <p>
             What you are really trying to say is that the American ideal of
a "right to long life" no matter the cost is simply impossible.
            </p>
            <p>
             We need to deregulate markets for health care today and allow
people to drink, smoke, and use any kind of drug they want.
            </p>

my responsibility to guarantee someone else all the health care
they can have in order to live as long as they like.
            </p>
            <p>
             The truth is this John. Under the free market, loads of
unhealthy poor people are going to die.
            </p>

            <p>
             Can we call you Liberals........Progressives? Screw all of you
liberal morons. You are willing to give this country away without a
shot being fired to acquire socialism/communism because you dont
want to work, you always have your hands out for something free,
paid for by someone else and you want big government to make your
decisions for you in everyday life. What a buch of whooses you
liberals are!
            </p>
            <p>
             Declaration of Tea Party Independence
            </p>
            <p>
             The tea party movement is not run from any central point. There
is no national, controlling apparatus, no top down structure, no
board of directors, no president, no head person of any kind in
charge of the tea party movement. In spite of what the
untrustworthy mainstream press or the corrupt political class has
attempted to portray, the tea party movement is a grass roots
movement which has grown up nearly spontaneously across the United
States in response to the overwhelming corruption of a cynical,
elitist, and criminal ruling class which has long since abandoned
the principles associated with the founding of this nation in favor
of a self serving and shameful aggrandisement of themselves and
their political associates. This ruling class has driven the people
of this country into a state of justifiable rebellion and we the
people have risen in response to state publicly that we have borne
the burden of an out of control government for as long as we can
reasonably be expected to do so. The founding fathers of this
nation set forth the principles under which we the people would
consent to be governed and the manner and means by which we could
regulate, and control our destiny and that of our nation. This
nation belongs to the people, not to any group of pretenders in any
capital anywhere in the land, and as it is our country, we have the
right to make whatever changes are necessary should it become
apparent that government has become destructive of our rights and
interests. The original Declaration Of Independence, the founding
document of our country, laid out for all the world to see, the
principles upon which this nation would forever cast its lot. In
that document, it clearly states,
            </p>
            <p>
             That whenever any Form of Government becomes destructive of
these ends (the God given, Natural rights of man), it is the Right
of the People to alter or to abolish it.
            </p>
            <p>
             We the people have never relinquished that right, and in spite
of the efforts of what has become largely a criminal class of
thieves, usurpers, and arrogant elitists, to prevent us from
exercising our rights as free Americans, we are coming forward on
this day to present this Declaration Of Tea Party Independence in
which we declare ourselves independent of the corrupt practices and
policies of the major political parties of this nation, to include
but not be limited to the Democrat and Republican parties and their
corrupt apparatus and apparatchiks. It is our intent to live as
free Americans, as much as possible, until such time as we can
recapture our nation from the thieves and despots whose long train
of usurious acts and usurpations have exacted an onerous and
unseemly toll upon the honest citizens of these United States of
America, so help us God.
            </p>
            <p>
             Amen.
            </p>

many bloggers do not get appreciation they deserve. I am sure I'll
drop by again and will send some of my friends.

      <script>
       $(document).ready(function() {
    	//no point in binding to swipe events if there's no touch support in the browser (and it goofs up selection)
		if ('ontouchstart' in window) {
			//in an effort to reduce false horizontal swipes from bold vertical flicks on larger screens...
			swipeThreshold = 200;
			$("#content-col").swipe( {
				threshold: swipeThreshold,
				allowPageScroll: 'vertical',
			    swipeLeft:function(event, direction, distance, duration, fingerCount) {
			    	//we're going to put in a non-zero fingercount check here to exclude mouse drags
					if (fingerCount &amp;&amp; $('#nextpage').length &amp;&amp; $('#nextpage').attr("href").length) {
					    window.location.href=  $('#nextpage').attr("href");
					}
			    },
			    swipeRight:function(event, direction, distance, duration, fingerCount) {
			    	//we're going to put in a non-zero fingercount check here to exclude mouse drags
					if (fingerCount &amp;&amp; $('#previouspage').length &amp;&amp; $('#previouspage').attr("href").length) {
				    	window.location.href = $('#previouspage').attr("href");
					}
			    }
			});
		}
    });
      </script>

         $(function(){
	$("#topstoriessidebar .selector a").click(function(e){
		var $this=$(this), catref = $this.attr("data-category"),
			$sidebar = $this.parent().parent().parent();
		e.preventDefault();
		$sidebar.find('&gt; .selector &gt; li').removeClass('active');
		$this.parent().addClass('active');
		$sidebar.find('&gt; .inner &gt; .stories').hide().filter('[data-category='+catref+']').show();
	});
});
